title: "Ubuntu not recognizing windows 7"
date: 2015-10-01
forum: New to Ubuntu

### Post by kevin184 on 2015-10-01
Hello everyone! 

I am a current IT Major and I've recently taken a great interest in trying Ubuntu.

I have Windows 7 SP1 Home Premium currently installed and working. My goal is to dual boot Ubuntu 14.0.4.
I have a USB stick with the installer on it. I've gotten my computer to recognize it as bootable device, and gotten all the way into the installer. I've had to use "nomodeset" to stop my screen from going black.
When I get the installer, everything is great until the installer does not recognize  that windows 7 is there at all. I'm very new to this, and could use any help you all are willing to offer.

Thanks you guys so much!

---

### Post by grahammechanical on 2015-10-01
For us to give accurate advice it would help if you used a Windows utility to display the partition layout of your hard drive and then take a screenshot and post it in your thread.

It is possible that your motherboard has a BIOS boot system with an msdos partition table and that means that you can only have 4 partitions (primary partitions) on the hard disk. If Microsift and the manufacturer together have used up the allowed 4 partitions then the installer cannot offer the Install Alongside option.

It could be that you need to delete at least one partition and resize another to create unallocation space. Then the Ubuntu installer can create a special type of primary partition called an Extended partition and in that Extended partition in turn create 2 Logical partitions, one for Ubuntu and one for swap.

A screenshot would give us a better idea of the situation. It is best to defrag the hard disk using Windows utilities and to do it more than once and restart each time. It is also best to use Windows utilities to delete and resize Windows partitions also restart to confirm that Windows still loads. Furthermore, you should have Windows restore disks.

If there is sufficent unallocated space and an unused allocation of at least one primary partition then the installer will offer the Install Alongside option.

Regards.

---

### Post by mastablasta on 2015-10-02
eh, just leave it. it might come in handy later on. if not there is not much space wasted anyway... make a bigger one at the end of that C:\ drive. make sure you defrag the drive before doing it. leave it unformatted and hopefully installer will pick it up. good luck.

edit: if you wish you can use the 100 MB partition as /boot partition (though this is not necessary).
